جارية وتقابضا فوجد بها عيباً فقال البائع بعتك هذه واخرى معها. وقال المشترى بعتنيها وحدها فالقول قول المشترى لان الاختلاف في مقدار المقبوض فيكون القول للقابض كما في الغصب وكذا اذا اتفقا على مقدار المبيع واختلفا في المقبوض لما بينا ترجمہ کہا اور اگر کسی نے باندی خریدی اور مشتری نے باندی پر اور بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ کر لیا پھر مشتری نے باندی کے اندر کوئی عیب پایا۔ پس بائع نے کہا کہ میں نے تیرے ہاتھ یہ باندی اور اس کے ساتھ دوسری باندی فروخت کی اور مشتری نے کہا تو نے میرے ہاتھ یہ اکیلی باندی فروخت کی ہے تو مشتری کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جس چیز پر قبضہ کیا گیا اس کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہے۔ لہذا قبضہ کرنے والے کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ جیسے غصب میں ہوتا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر دونوں نے مبیع کی مقدار پر اتفاق کیا اور مقبوض کی مقدار میں اختلاف کیا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایک باندی خریدی اور مشتری نے باندی پر اور بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ کر لیا پھر مشتری کو باندی کے اندر کوئی عیب محسوس ہوا تو مشتری نے باندی واپس کر کے پورا شمن واپس لینا چاہا بیس بائع نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ باندی یقینا فروخت کی تھی لیکن اس کے ساتھ ایک باندی اور فروخت کی تھی اسلئے تم کو معیب باندی واپس کر کے اس کے حصہ کے بقدر ثمن واپس لینے کا اختیار ہے پورا شمن واپس لینے کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ مشتری نے کہا کہ تو نے میرے ساتھ فقط یہی ایک باندی فروخت کی ہے اسلئے پورا شمن واپس لوں گا اور اتفاق سے گواہ کسی کے پاس نہیں ہیں تو ایسی صورت میں مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ جس چیز پر قبضہ کیا گیا ہے اس کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بائع دعویٰ کرتا ہے کہ مشتری نے دو باندیوں پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور مشتری کہتا ہے کہ میں نے ایک باندی پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور مقدار مقبوض کے اندر اختلاف کی صورت میں قابض ہی کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے قابض خواہ امین ہو یا ضمین ہو اس لئے کہ غیر قابض یعنی قبضہ دینے والا مثلا بائع زیادتی کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے اور قابض یعنی قبضہ کرنے والا مثلاً مشتری زیادتی کا انکار کرتا ہے اور بینہ کسی کے پاس موجود نہیں ہے تو منکر یعنی قابض کا قول قبول کیا جائے گا جیسا کہ غاصب اور مغصوب منہ کے درمیان اختلاف کی صورت میں ہے۔ مغصوب منہ نے کہا کہ تو نے میرے دو غلام غصب کئے ہیں اور غاصب نے کہا کہ میں نے ایک غلام غصب کیا ہے تو مقدار مقبوض کے سلسلے میں غاصب کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ غاصب ہی قابض ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ قابض کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے اسلئے غاصب کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر بائع اور مشتری دونوں نے مبیع کی مقدار پر تو اتفاق کیا کہ مبیع دو باندی ہیں لیکن مقدار مقبوض میں اختلاف کیا باایں طور کہ بائع کہتا ہے کہ مشتری نے دونوں پر قبضہ کر لیا ہے اور مشتری کہتا ہے کہ میں نے فقط ایک باندی پر قبضہ کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی
A slave girl was purchased, and possession of the slave girl and the price was taken. Then the buyer found a defect. The seller says: 'I sold this and another slave girl with her.' The buyer says: 'You sold me only this one alone.' Whose statement will be accepted? He said: And if someone bought a slave girl, and they took mutual possession, then he found a defect in her, and the seller said: 'I sold you this and another with her,' and the buyer said: 'You sold me only her alone,' then the statement of the buyer is accepted because the dispute is over the quantity of what was taken possession. Thus the statement of the possessor is accepted, as in ghasb. Similarly, if they agree on the quantity sold but differ on the quantity taken possession, for the reason we have stated. Translation: He said: And if someone bought a slave girl, and the buyer took possession of the slave girl and the seller took possession of the price, then the buyer found a defect in the slave girl. So the seller said: 'I sold to you this slave girl and another with her,' and the buyer said: 'You sold me only this one slave girl.' Then the buyer's statement will be accepted. Because there is a dispute about the quantity of what was taken possession. Therefore the statement of the possessor will be accepted, as in ghasb. And similarly if both agreed on the quantity of the sold item but differed on the quantity taken possession, for the reason we have stated. Explanation: The scenario of the issue is that a person bought a slave girl, and the buyer took possession of the slave girl and the seller took possession of the price. Then the buyer felt a defect in the slave girl, so he wanted to return the slave girl and take back the full price. The seller said: 'I certainly sold this slave girl, but I also sold another slave girl with her. Therefore you have the option to return the defective slave girl and take back the price proportionate to her share, but you have no right to take back the full price.' The buyer said: 'You sold me only this one slave girl, so I will take back the full price.' And by chance, neither has witnesses. In such a case, the buyer's statement will be accepted because there is a dispute about the quantity of what was taken possession. Thus the seller claims that the buyer took possession of two slave girls, and the buyer says he took possession of one slave girl. In a dispute over the quantity of possession, the statement of the possessor is accepted, whether the possessor is an amin (trustee) or a damin (liable). Because the non-possessor, i.e., the one who gave possession, e.g., the seller, claims an excess, and the possessor, i.e., the one who took possession, e.g., the buyer, denies the excess, and neither has evidence. So the denier, i.e., the possessor, his statement will be accepted, as in the dispute between the usurper and the usurped-from. The usurped-from said: 'You usurped two of my slaves,' and the usurper said: 'I usurped one slave.' Then in the matter of the quantity of possession, the statement of the usurper will be accepted because he is the possessor. And it has passed earlier that the statement of the possessor is accepted. Therefore the usurper's statement will be accepted. And similarly, if both the seller and the buyer agreed on the quantity of the sold item, that the sold item is two slave girls, but they differed on the quantity taken possession, in the manner that the seller says that the buyer took possession of both, and the buyer says that he took possession of only one slave girl, then in this case also [the buyer's statement is accepted].
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a dispute concerning the quantity of the item taken possession in a sale. The scenario: a buyer purchases a slave girl, takes possession, and then finds a defect. The seller claims he sold two slave girls (the defective one and another), while the buyer claims he only purchased one. The ruling is that the buyer's statement is accepted because the dispute is about the quantity of what was 'possessed' (maqbud). The possessor (qabid) is the buyer, and his denial of the excess is accepted over the seller's claim of excess. The author supports this ruling by analogy to ghasb (usurpation): if the usurped-from claims two slaves were usurped but the usurper admits to only one, the usurper's statement is accepted because he is the possessor. The same applies whether the possessor is an amin (trustee) or a damin (liable). The passage also applies the same rule when both parties agree on the quantity sold but differ on the quantity taken possession: the possessor's statement is accepted. This ruling is based on the principle that in disputes over the quantity of possession, the possessor's denial of excess is preferred over the non-possessor's claim of excess, in the absence of evidence.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of the sold item; legal possession.
قابض (qabid): The person who takes possession; the possessor.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation of another's property without right.
امین (amin): A trustee who holds property without liability for loss except in case of negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the buyer's statement accepted in the dispute over the quantity of slave girls taken possession?
A) Because the buyer is the owner after sale.
B) Because the buyer denies the excess and is the possessor.
C) Because the seller is not a reliable witness.
D) Because the slave girl is defective.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when possession is taken, the possessor's denial of excess is accepted over the non-possessor's claim of excess in disputes over quantity of possession.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Dispute over Quantity Received in a Sale
Determining whose statement is believed when buyer and seller dispute the quantity received.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when buyer and seller dispute the quantity received, identify the analogy from ghasb, and apply the rule to two related scenarios.

Core Idea
In a dispute over quantity received, the receiver’s statement is believed, by analogy with usurpation.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical dispute after a sale: the seller claims he delivered two slave-girls, the buyer claims only one. How is this resolved? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on possession and an analogy with ghasb (usurpation). We will analyze the ruling, its proof from qiyas, and a related second scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The seller claims he sold two slave-girls and delivered both; the buyer admits only one. No witnesses are available.
The dispute centers on the quantity of the received goods (مقدار المقبوض).
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that the buyer's (receiver's) statement is accepted. The buyer can return the defective slave-girl for a full refund.
The rule is: في مقدار المقبوض فالقول للقابض.
3
Trace the proof
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to ghasb (usurpation). In ghasb, the usurper's statement about the quantity taken is believed because he is the possessor.
The text says: كما في الغصب.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The common 'illa (effective cause) is that the receiver is in possession and the other party claims an excess; the denier's statement is accepted. The non-receiver is the claimant of an increase.
This principle applies whether the receiver is a trustee (amin) or a guarantor (damin).
5
Apply to the second scenario
If both agree that the sale contract was for two slave-girls but dispute how many were actually delivered, the receiver's statement (buyer) is still believed.
The proof is the same: the dispute is over the quantity of the received goods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اشترى جارية وتقابضا فوجد بها عيبا فقال البائع بعتك هذه وأخرى معها. وقال المشتري بعتنيها وحدها فالقول قول المشتري لان الاختلاف في مقدار المقبوض فيكون القول للقابض كما في الغصب وكذا إذا اتفقا على مقدار المبيع واختلفا في المقبوض لما بينا.
ترجمہ: کہا اور اگر کسی نے باندی خریدی اور مشتری نے باندی پر اور بائع نے ثمن پر قبضہ کر لیا پھر مشتری نے باندی کے اندر کوئی عیب پایا۔ پس بائع نے کہا کہ میں نے تیرے ہاتھ یہ باندی اور اس کے ساتھ دوسری باندی فروخت کی اور مشتری نے کہا تو نے میرے ہاتھ یہ اکیلی باندی فروخت کی ہے تو مشتری کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جس چیز پر قبضہ کیا گیا اس کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہے۔ لہذا قبضہ کرنے والے کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ جیسے غصب میں ہوتا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر دونوں نے مبیع کی مقدار پر اتفاق کیا اور مقبوض کی مقدار میں اختلاف کیا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایک باندی خریدی اور مشتری نے باندی پر اور بائع نے ثمن پر قبضہ کر لیا پھر مشتری کو باندی کے اندر کوئی عیب محسوس ہوا تو مشتری نے باندی واپس کر کے پورا ثمن واپس لینا چاہا۔ بائع نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ باندی یقینا فروخت کی تھی لیکن اس کے ساتھ ایک باندی اور فروخت کی تھی اس لئے تم کو معیب باندی واپس کر کے اس کے حصہ کے بقدر ثمن واپس لینے کا اختیار ہے پورا ثمن واپس لینے کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ مشتری نے کہا کہ تو نے میرے ساتھ فقط یہی ایک باندی فروخت کی ہے اس لئے پورا ثمن واپس لوں گا اور اتفاق سے گواہ کسی کے پاس نہیں ہیں تو ایسی صورت میں مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ جس چیز پر قبضہ کیا گیا ہے اس کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بائع دعوی کرتا ہے کہ مشتری نے دو باندیوں پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور مشتری کہتا ہے کہ میں نے ایک باندی پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور مقدار مقبوض کے اندر اختلاف کی صورت میں قابض ہی کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے قابض خواہ امین ہو یا ضمین ہو اس لئے کہ غیر قابض یعنی قبضہ دینے والا مثلا بائع زیادتی کا دعوی کرتا ہے اور قابض یعنی قبضہ کرنے والا مثلاً مشتری زیادتی کا انکار کرتا ہے اور بینہ کسی کے پاس موجود نہیں ہے تو منکر یعنی قابض کا قول قبول کیا جائے گا جیسا کہ غاصب اور مغصوب منہ کے درمیان اختلاف کی صورت میں ہے۔ مغصوب منہ نے کہا کہ تو نے میرے دو غلام غصب کئے ہیں اور غاصب نے کہا کہ میں نے ایک غلام غصب کیا ہے تو مقدار مقبوض کے سلسلے میں غاصب کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ غاصب ہی قابض ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ قابض کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے اس لئے غاصب کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر بائع اور مشتری دونوں نے مبیع کی مقدار پر تو اتفاق کیا کہ مبیع دو باندی ہیں لیکن مقدار مقبوض میں اختلاف کیا با ایں طور کہ بائع کہتا ہے کہ مشتری نے دونوں پر قبضہ کر لیا ہے اور مشتری کہتا ہے کہ میں نے فقط ایک باندی پر قبضہ کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی چونکہ مشتری قابض ہے اس لئے اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا
He said: And if one buys a slave-girl, and they exchange possession (the buyer takes the slave-girl and the seller takes the price), then he finds a defect in her, and the seller says: 'I sold you this one and another with her,' and the buyer says: 'You sold me only her alone,' then the statement is the buyer's statement because the dispute is about the quantity of what was received, so the statement is for the receiver, just as in usurpation (ghasb). Likewise, if they agree on the quantity of the sold item but dispute the quantity received, based on what we have explained.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah. The passage addresses a dispute between buyer and seller after a sale of a slave-girl. The seller claims he sold two slave-girls together, while the buyer claims only one. Both have exchanged possession (buyer received the slave-girl, seller received the price). The buyer later finds a defect and wants to return the slave-girl for a full refund. The key issue is the quantity of what was received by the buyer. The rule is: in a dispute over the quantity of received goods, the statement of the receiver (the buyer) is believed. This is based on analogy (qiyas) with ghasb (usurpation): if the owner claims two slaves were usurped and the usurper admits only one, the usurper's statement is believed because he is the possessor. Similarly, the buyer is the possessor of the received goods. The commentary explains that this applies whether the receiver is a trustee (amin) or a guarantor (damin), because the non-receiver (seller) is claiming an excess and the receiver is denying it, and the denier's statement is accepted. The proof is that the seller claims an increase, the buyer denies it, and without evidence, the denier's statement prevails. This ruling also applies if both agree on the quantity of the sale contract (e.g., two slave-girls) but disagree on how many were actually received: the receiver's statement is still taken.

Key Terms
قابض (qabid): The one who takes possession (receiver), i.e., the buyer in this context.
مقبوض (maqbud): The object that has been taken possession of, i.e., the received goods.
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful usurpation of property; used here as an analogy for sale disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over how many items were received in a sale, whose statement is accepted according to this Hanafi ruling?
A) The seller's
B) The buyer's
C) The witness's
D) The judge's

Key Takeaway
In disputes over the quantity of goods received, the Hanafi school accepts the statement of the receiver (buyer), by analogy with the ruling in cases of usurpation.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Returning a Defective Item Before Full Receipt in a Single Sale
Ruling on returning a defective slave when two are sold together and only one is received

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a buyer finds a defect in an unreceived item from a single sale of two items, and explain the reasoning based on completion of the contract (safqah).

Core Idea
In a single sale, the contract is completed only by receipt of all items; returning one before that separates the contract before completion.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in sales: when multiple items are sold together in one contract. The key question is whether a buyer can return only a defective item if he has not yet received all items. The Hanafi ruling hinges on when the contract is considered complete. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the concept of tafriq al-safqah (separation of the contract) and the role of possession (qabd) in completing the sale for different options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is buying two slaves in one contract, receiving one, and finding a defect in the unreceived one. The Hanafi ruling: the buyer must either take both or return both. He cannot return only the defective one.
The ruling is procedural (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is that the contract (safqah) is completed only by taking possession of all items. Returning one before that would be tafriq al-safqah (separating the contract) before its completion, which is prohibited.
The dalil is based on analogy: possession is like the contract itself.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key analogy: just as one cannot separate the items in the contract (e.g., return one at the time of contracting), one cannot separate them in possession. Therefore, returning only one unreceived item is equivalent to separating the contract before completion.
This analogy is drawn from the similarity between qabd (possession) and aqd (contract).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: a narration from Abu Yusuf allows returning only the received defective slave. However, the relied-upon view (asahh) is to take or return both. Also, after full receipt, there is a dispute with Imam Zufar who prohibits returning only one.
These differences arise from different views on when the sale is considered complete.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that possession completes the sale for khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) but not for khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight) or khiyar al-shart (option of condition). Hence, after full receipt, returning only the defective one is allowed.
This distinction is crucial and is cited as the Hanafi response to Zufar.

قال ومن اشترى عبدين صفقة واحدة فقبض أحدهما ووجد بالآخر عيبا فإنه يأخذهما أو يردهما لأن الصفقة تتم بقبضهما فيكون تفريقهما قبل التمام وقد ذكرناه وهذا لأن القبض له شبه بالعقد فالتفريق فيه كالتفريق في العقد ولو وجد بالمقبوض عيبا اختلفوا فيه ويروى عن أبي يوسف أنه يرده خاصة والأصح أنه يأخذهما أو يردهما لأن تمام الصفقة تعلق بقبض المبيع وهو اسم للكل فصار كحبس المبيع لما تعلق زواله باستيفاء الثمن لايزول دون قبض جميعه ولو قبضهما ثم وجد بأحدهما عيبا يرده خاصة خلافا لزفر هو يقول فيه تفريق الصفقة ولا يعرى عن ضرر لأن العادة بضم الجيد إلى الردي فشبه ما قبل القبض وخيار الرؤية والشرط ولنا أنه تفريق الصفقة بعد التمام لأن بالقبض تتم الصفقة في خيار العيب وفي خيار الرؤية والشرط لم تتم به على ما مر وهذه الواو استحق أحدهما ليس له أن يرد الآخر.
ترجمہ: کہا کہ اگر کسی نے دو غلام ایک عقد کے تحت خریدے۔ پس ان دونوں میں سے ایک پر قبضہ کر لیا اور دوسرے میں کوئی عیب پایا تو دونوں غلاموں کو لے لے یا دونوں کو واپس کردے کیونکہ صفقہ دونوں پر قبضہ کرنے سے تمام ہوگا۔ پس (ایک کو واپس کرنے سے ) تفریق صفقہ قبل التمام لازم آئے گا۔ اور ہم اس کو پہلے ذکر کر چکے۔ اور یہ اسلئے ہے کہ قبضہ، عقد کے مشابہ ہے لہذا قبضہ میں تمام تفریق کرنا عقد کی تفریق کے مانند ہے اور اگر اس نے غلام مقبوض میں عیب پایا تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے اور ابو یوسف سے روایت کی جاتی ہے کہ فقط مقبوض کو واپس کرے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو لے یا دونوں کو واپس کرے کیونکہ صفقہ کا مکمل ہونا مبیع کے قبضہ کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور مبیع کل کا نام ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ مبیع کو روکنا جبکہ مبیع روکنے کا زائل ہونا ثمن وصول کرنے کے ساتھ متعلق ہو تو مبیع روکنے کا حق پورے ثمن پر قبضہ کئے بغیر زائل نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر دونوں غلاموں پر قبضہ کیا پھر ایک میں عیب پایا تو فقط اس کو واپس کر دے اس میں امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے وہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس میں بھی تفریق صفقہ ہے اور ضرر سے خالی نہیں ہے کیونکہ عادت یہ جاری ہے کہ ردی کے ساتھ جید کو ملا دیتے ہیں۔ پس یہ قبضہ سے پہلے یا خیار رویت یا خیار شرط کی وجہ سے (ایک کو واپس کرنے کے ) مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں صفقہ تمام ہونے کے بعد تفریق صفقہ ہے کیونکہ خیار عیب میں قبضہ سے صفقہ تمام ہو جاتا ہے اور خیار رویت اور خیار شرط میں قبضہ سے صفقہ تمام نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ سابق میں گذر چکا اسی وجہ سے اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک مستحق ہو گیا تو مشتری کیلئے دوسرے کو واپس کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے عقد واحد کے تحت دو غلام خریدے مثلاً بائع نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ دونوں غلام ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض تیرے ہاتھ فروخت کئے مشتری نے قبول کر لیا اور ان میں سے ایک غلام پر ( جو کہ بے عیب تھا ) قبضہ کیا اور دوسرے میں کوئی عیب نظر آیا تو مشتری کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ معیب غلام کو واپس کر دے اور سلیم ( بے عیب ) کو لے لے بلکہ پورے ثمن کے عوض دونوں کو
He said: And if one buys two slaves in one contract, then takes possession of one of them and finds a defect in the other, then he must take both or return both, because the contract is completed by taking possession of both, so separating them before completion is not allowed, as we have mentioned. And this is because possession is similar to the contract, so separating in possession is like separating in the contract. And if he finds a defect in the received one, there is disagreement among the scholars; it is related from Abu Yusuf that he returns only that one, but the more correct view is that he takes both or returns both, because the completion of the contract is tied to possession of the sold item, and 'sold item' is a name for the whole, so it becomes like detention of the sold item: since its removal is tied to receipt of the price, it does not cease without receipt of all. And if he takes possession of both, then finds a defect in one, he returns only that one, contrary to Zufar who says: here too is separation of the contract and it involves harm, because the custom is to join the good with the bad, so it resembles the case before possession and the options of sight and condition. Our proof is that here the separation is after completion, because in the option of defect, the contract is completed by possession, whereas in the options of sight and condition, it is not completed by possession, as previously mentioned. For this reason, if one of them is found to be owned by another, the buyer cannot return the other.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling from the Hidayah on a sale of two items in one contract. The core issue: if a buyer receives one slave and finds a defect in the unreceived one, he cannot return only the defective one; he must return both or keep both. This is because the contract (safqah) is completed only upon receipt of all items; returning one before full receipt would be separation of the contract before completion, which is prohibited. This is analogous to the contract itself: just as one cannot separate the items in the contract, one cannot separate them in possession. The commentary addresses a sub-case: if the defect is in the received slave, there is ikhtilaf. A narration from Abu Yusuf allows returning only the received defective one, but the relied-upon (asahh) view is the same as before: take both or return both. The reasoning is that the completion of the sale is tied to possession of the entire sold item (mabi'), and possession of part does not complete it. Another sub-case: if both slaves are received and then a defect is found in one, the buyer may return only that one. This is the Hanafi position, opposing Imam Zufar who says it constitutes separation of the contract and causes harm because combining good and bad is customary. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), possession completes the sale, so returning after possession is separation after completion, which is allowed. In the options of sight and condition, possession does not complete the sale, so returning before completion would be separation before completion. This distinction is the key. Additionally, if one slave turns out to be owned by another (i.e., not the seller's), the buyer cannot return the other slave; he only returns the one that was not owned.

Key Terms
صفقة (safqah): The entire contract or transaction; completing the safqah means the sale is fully executed.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession; in this context, it completes the sale for khiyar al-'ayb but not for khiyar al-ru'yah or khiyar al-shart.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option to return due to a defect; possession completes the sale for this option according to the Hanafi view.
تفريق الصفقة (tafriq al-safqah): Separating the parts of a single sale transaction, which is prohibited if done before completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi sale of two items in one contract, if the buyer receives one and finds a defect in the unreceived one, what are his options?
A) Return only the defective one
B) Keep both or return both
C) Keep the received one and return the defective one
D) He must keep both

Key Takeaway
In a single sale, the contract is completed only by receipt of all items; returning an unreceived defective item alone separates the contract before completion.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Unity of the Contract and Return of Defective Items Before Full Possession
Ruling on the effect of possession on the unity of the sale contract regarding defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on tafriq al-safqah (splitting the transaction) before full possession and explain the intra-Hanafi disputes regarding khiyar al-'ayb.

Core Idea
A single contract requires full possession of all items before partial return is allowed.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common commercial scenario: buying multiple items in one contract, taking possession of only some, and later discovering a defect. The central legal question is whether the buyer may return only the defective item or must return the whole lot. The ruling hinges on the concept of tafriq al-safqah—splitting a single transaction before its completion—which is prohibited. The passage also examines differing views within the Hanafi school, providing a rich opportunity to understand how classical jurists balanced contractual unity with the buyer's right to reject defective goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Read the opening sentence of the passage carefully. It states the rule when a buyer purchases two items in one transaction, takes possession of one, and finds a defect in the other. Determine what the buyer must do and note the condition (possession of only one) that triggers this ruling.
2
Understand the Rationale via Qiyas
The author draws an analogy (qiyas jaliy) between possession and the contract itself. Explain this analogy: how does possession resemble the contract in establishing legal effects, and why does splitting in possession mirror splitting in the contract?
This is a key methodological tool in Hanafi fiqh: using qiyas to extend a ruling from the contract to possession.
3
Analyze the First Dispute: Defect in the Possessed Slave
The passage presents a narration from Abu Yusuf allowing the buyer to return only the defective slave if the defect is in the possessed one. Contrast this with the majority (correct) opinion that requires returning both. Identify the reasoning behind each view.
Abu Yusuf's view treats possession of an item as completing the contract for that item; the majority views the contract as indivisible until all items are possessed.
4
Analyze the Second Dispute: Defect After Full Possession
After full possession of both slaves, the buyer may return only the defective one. Imam Zufar objects, arguing that this still splits the transaction and harms the seller due to custom (mixing good with bad). Understand Zufar's proof and the majority's refutation based on the distinction between khiyar al-'ayb and other options.
The distinction between khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'ya or khiyar al-shart is critical: in the latter, possession does not complete the contract.
5
Apply to a Related Case: Istihqaq
The passage ends with a related ruling: if one slave is rightfully claimed by a third party, the buyer cannot return the other slave. Explain why this follows the same principle of transaction unity.
This reinforces that the buyer cannot unilaterally split the transaction once external events affect the contract.

عیب پایا جس پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور دوسرا غلام جس پر قبضہ نہیں کیا وہ عیب سے سلیم ہے۔ تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ مشتری خاص طور سے غلام معیب کو واپس کر کے اس کا حصہ ثمن لے لے اور غیر معیب کو واپس نہ کرے کیونکہ غلام مقبوض کے حق میں صفقہ تمام ہو گیا ہے۔ پس غلام مقبوض کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے تفریق صفقہ لازم نہیں آیا اور جب تفریق صفقہ لازم نہیں آیا تو اس کے جائز ہونے میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے لیکن اصح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی مشتری پورے شمن کے عوض دونوں غلام لے لے یا دونوں کو واپس کر دے کیونکہ صفقہ کا پورا ہونا مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے کے ساتھ متعلق ہے یعنی مشتری کے مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد ہی صفقہ پورا ہوگا اور مبیع اس کل کا نام ہے جس پر عقد بیع واقع ہوا ہے اور عقد بیع دو غلاموں پر واقع ہوا ہے لہذا دونوں غلاموں پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد ہی صفقہ پورا ہو گا اور مذکورہ صورت میں چونکہ ایک غلام پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور ایک پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اسلئے اس صورت میں صفقہ پورا نہیں ہوا اور جب صفقہ پورا نہیں ہوا تو ایک غلام کو واپس کرنے میں تفریق صفقہ قبل التمام لازم آئے گا اور تفریق صفتہ قبل التمام نا جائز ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں بھی ایک غلام کو واپس کرنا اور ایک کو واپس نہ کرنا نا جائز ہوگا اور بیچ اس کل کا نام ہے جس پر بیچ واقع ہوئی۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر بائع نے بیع کو اپنے پاس اسلئے روک لیا کہ مشتری جب ثمن ادا کرے گا تو میں مبیع سپر د کروں گا۔ پس بائع کا یہ حق اس وقت تک زائل نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ مشتری پورا شمن ادا نہ کرے چنانچہ مشتری نے اگر کچھ شمن ادا کیا تو بھی بائع کو بیچ روکنے کا حق حاصل ہے کیونکہ شمشن پورے عوض کا نام ہے نہ کہ بعض عوض کا اسی طرح صبیح بھی پورے معوض کا نام ہے نہ کہ بعض معوض کا اور اگر مشتری نے دونوں غلاموں پر قبضہ کر لیا پھر ان میں سے ایک میں عیب پایا تو یہ فقط معیب کو اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں بھی دونوں غلام واپس کرے یا دونوں کو لے ۔ خاص طور سے ایک کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی تفریق صفقہ ہے اگر چہ بعد التمام ہے اور اس میں بائع کا ضرر ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کی عادت یہ ہے کہ وہ جید کے ساتھ ردی کو ملا کر فروخت کرتے ہیں۔ پس اگر مشتری کو ایک غلام واپس کرنے کی اجازت دے دی گئی تو بائع کا نقصان ہوگا بایں طور کہ مشتری نے جو قلام واپس کیا وہ ردی ہوا اور جید کو اپنے پاس روک لیا ہو تو بائع کیلئے تنہا اس روئی غلام کو بیچنا دشوار ہوگا پس بائع سے ضرر دور کرنے کے واسطے فقط معیب
He said: If one buys two slaves in a single transaction and takes possession of one of them and finds a defect in the other, then he either takes both or returns both, because the transaction is completed by taking possession of both, so splitting them before completion [occurs]. And we have mentioned this. And this is because possession has a resemblance to the contract, so splitting in it is like splitting the contract. And if he finds a defect in the possessed [slave], they differed about it. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he returns it specifically. And the most correct is that he takes both or returns both, because the completion of the transaction is connected to possession of the sold item, and it is a name for the whole, so it becomes like retention of the sold item, the removal of which is connected to full receipt of the price, not removing without taking possession of it all. And if he took possession of both then found a defect in one, he returns it specifically, contrary to Zufar. He says: There is splitting of the transaction and it is not free from harm, because the custom is to mix the good with the bad, so it resembles [the case] before possession and the option of inspection and stipulation. And our proof: It is splitting the transaction after completion, because with possession the transaction is completed in the option of defect, while in the option of inspection and stipulation it is not completed. And this is as passed. And if one of them is claimed by a third party, he has no right to return the other. Translation: He said that if someone purchased two slaves under one contract, then took possession of one of them and found a defect in the other, then he should take both slaves or return both, because the transaction will be completed only after taking possession of both. So returning one would entail splitting the transaction before completion, which is impermissible. This is because possession resembles the contract, so splitting in possession is like splitting the contract. And if he found a defect in the possessed slave, there is disagreement among the scholars. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he returns only the possessed one, but the correct view is that he takes both or returns both, because the completion of the transaction is linked to possession of the sold item, and 'sold item' is a name for the whole. So it becomes like the seller's retention of the sold item, whose removal is linked to receipt of the full price; it is not removed without taking possession of all of it. And if he took possession of both then found a defect in one, he returns only that one, contrary to Imam Zufar. He says that this also entails splitting of the transaction and is not free from harm, because the custom is to mix the good with the bad, so it resembles the case before possession or due to option of inspection or stipulation. Our proof is that here the transaction is split after completion, because in the option of defect, possession completes the transaction, whereas in the option of inspection and stipulation, possession does not complete it, as previously mentioned. Therefore, if one of them is claimed by a rightful owner, the buyer does not have the right to return the other. Explanation of the issue: If a person bought two slaves in a single contract, e.g., the seller said 'I sold you these two slaves for one thousand dirhams,' and the buyer accepted, and he took possession of one slave (which was defect-free) and found a defect in the other, then the buyer does not have the right to return the defective slave and keep the sound one; rather, he must either take both for the full price or return both. The proof is that in the case of the option of defect, the transaction is completed only after possession, not before. So in this issue, the transaction will be completed only when the buyer takes possession of both slaves, but he has only taken possession of one. Thus, returning the defective one and keeping the sound one constitutes splitting the transaction before completion, which is impermissible. Splitting the transaction in possession is impermissible because possession resembles the contract in that the contract establishes ownership of the substance (milk al-raqabah), while possession establishes ownership of disposal (milk al-tasarruf) and physical control (milk al-yad). Since both aim to establish ownership of disposal and control, they resemble each other. Therefore, splitting the transaction in possession is like splitting it in the contract, and splitting the contract is impermissible. An example of splitting the contract is if a seller said 'I sold these two slaves for one thousand dirhams,' and the buyer said 'I accept the sale of one slave,' this is not valid. Similarly, taking possession of one and returning the other due to a defect is not valid. And if the buyer found a defect in the slave he possessed while the other slave (not possessed) was sound, there is disagreement among the scholars. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that the buyer specifically returns the defective slave and takes his share of the price, and does not return the sound one, because regarding the possessed slave, the transaction is complete. Thus, no splitting of the transaction is necessitated. However, the soundest opinion is that even in this case, the buyer must take both for the full price or return both, because the completion of the transaction is linked to possession of all the sold items. The sold item is a name for the whole subject of the contract. Since the contract was on two slaves, the transaction is complete only upon possession of both. In this case, since he has taken possession of only one, the transaction is not complete, so returning one would necessitate splitting before completion, which is impermissible. Analogous to this is that if the seller retains the sold item until the buyer pays the price, this right of retention is not removed until the full price is paid. Paying part does not remove it, because 'price' denotes the whole, not part. Similarly, 'sold item' denotes the whole, not part. And if the buyer took possession of both slaves then found a defect in one, he can return only that defective one for its share of the price. Imam Zufar holds that even in this case, he must return both or keep both; he does not have the option to return just one. Zufar's proof is that this too involves splitting the transaction, albeit after completion, and it causes harm to the seller because people customarily mix the good with the bad. So if the buyer is allowed to return one slave, the seller would be harmed because the returned slave is the defective one and the buyer kept the good one, making it difficult for the seller to sell the defective one alone. Therefore, to prevent harm to the seller, only the defective one can be returned.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah, explaining the effect of possession on the unity of a sale contract when a defect is found. The key principle is that a single contract (safqah wahidah) is considered a single legal unit, and its completion is contingent on taking possession of all items sold. The author begins by stating the general rule: if a person buys two slaves in one transaction, takes possession of one, and finds a defect in the other, he may not return only the defective one; he must either return both or keep both. The reason is that the transaction is completed only by possession of both, and returning one before that would split the transaction before completion, which is prohibited. This is supported by an analogy: possession itself resembles the contract; just as splitting the contract (e.g., accepting only part of the offer) is invalid, splitting during possession before full possession is also invalid. The author then addresses two specific scenarios with intra-Hanafi disputes. First, if the defect is found in the possessed slave (the one already taken), there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that the buyer may return only that one, as the contract is complete regarding that slave. The correct opinion, however, is that the same rule applies: return both or keep both. The text analogizes to the seller's right to retain the goods until full payment of the price; the right is not removed until the full price is paid, just as the transaction is not complete until all items are possessed. Second, if the buyer possesses both slaves and then finds a defect in one, he may return only the defective one. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that returning one even after full possession splits the transaction and harms the seller due to custom (mixing good with bad). The majority refutes this, noting that after completion, splitting is allowed in the option of defect, as opposed to the option of inspection (where sight completes the contract). The author also notes a related case: if one of the slaves is rightfully claimed by a third party, the buyer cannot return the other slave. The commentary then elaborates with examples and reasoning, emphasizing that the 'sold item' (mabi') is a name for the whole, so partial return is impermissible before full possession. The relied-upon opinion is the majority view: the buyer must return both or keep both in all cases except after full possession of both, where only the defective one is returned.

Key Terms
صفقة (safqah): A single transaction or contract, encompassing all items sold under one agreement.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of an item sold, which completes the transfer of ownership for the purpose of liability and option of defect.
تفريق الصفقة (tafriq al-safqah): Splitting the single transaction by returning or accepting part of the goods, which is prohibited before the transaction is fully completed.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to return a defective item purchased, subject to conditions such as immediate discovery and no subsequent use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zayd buys two sheep in one contract. He takes possession of one sheep and finds a defect in the other. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what must Zayd do?
A) Return only the defective sheep and keep the sound one.
B) Keep both sheep and pay the full price.
C) Return both sheep or keep both sheep.
D) Return the sound sheep and keep the defective one.

Key Takeaway
A single transaction is not completed until all items are possessed; therefore, before full possession, the buyer must return all or keep all when a defect appears, but after full possession, only the defective item may be returned.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Returning a Defective Slave in a Multi-Item Sale: The Principle of Tafriq al-Safqah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tafriq al-safqah in khiyar al-'ayb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on partial return (tafriq al-safqah) in khiyar al-'ayb by distinguishing between pre- and post-possession scenarios.

Core Idea
In a multi-item sale, partial return is permitted only after full possession of all items completes the contract.

When you buy two items for one price and one is defective, can you return just that one? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced rule tied to possession. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar, centering on the concept of tafriq al-safqah (division of the contract). Understanding this principle is key to applying khiyar al-'ayb correctly in any multi-item transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
State the case: two slaves sold for one price; buyer finds a defect in one. The central question: can the buyer return only the defective slave and keep the other?
The answer varies with possession status.
2
Distinguish possession status
Note whether the buyer has taken possession of both slaves, only one, or none. This determines whether the contract (safqah) is complete.
Possession completes the contract only in khiyar al-'ayb, not in khiyar al-ru'yah or khiyar al-shart.
3
Outline the three Hanafi positions
Identify the views of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), Abu Yusuf, and Zufar. Understand the basis for each: Abu Hanifa links completion to full possession; Abu Yusuf considers possession of one sufficient; Zufar prohibits all partial return even after full possession to prevent harm.
The more correct view (al-qaul al-asahh) is the majority view.
4
Follow the reasoning for the majority view
Trace the argument: Before full possession, the safqah is incomplete; returning one slave is tafriq qabl al-tamam, which is invalid. After full possession, safqah is complete; tafriq ba'd al-tamam is valid.
The analogy with khiyar al-ru'yah fails because in those options, possession does not complete the contract.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: before full possession, the buyer must return all or keep all; after full possession, he may return only the defective one. This distinguishes the operative fatwa from the minority views.
The passage also applies this rule to cases of third-party claims (istihqaq).

کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی تفریق صفقہ ہے اگر چہ بعد التمام ہے اور اس میں بائع کا ضرر ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کی عادت یہ ہے کہ وہ جید کے ساتھ ردی کو ملا کر فروخت کرتے ہیں۔ پس اگر مشتری کو ایک غلام واپس کرنے کی اجازت دے دی گئی تو بائع کا نقصان ہوگا بایں طور کہ مشتری نے جو غلام واپس کیا وہ ردی ہوا اور جید کو اپنے پاس روک لیا ہو تو بائع کیلئے تنہا اس ردی غلام کو بیچنا دشوار ہوگا پس بائع سے ضرر دور کرنے کے واسطے فقط معیب غلام کو واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی اور یہ مابعد القبض کی صورت ماقبل القبض کے مشابہ ہوگئی اور ان دونوں کے درمیان جامع دفع ضرر ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بائع سے ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے فقط غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے کی اجازت قبضہ کرنے کے بعد بھی فقط غلام معیب واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے اسی طرح بائع سے ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے قبضہ کرنے کے بعد بھی فقط غلام معیب واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی اور یہ خیار رویت اور خیار شرط کے مشابہ ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح خیار رویت اور مشتری کے واسطے خیار شرط کی وجہ سے دو غلاموں میں سے ایک کو اپنے پاس رکھنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے اسی طرح ما بعد القبض غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے اور غیر معیب کو اپنے پاس رکھنے کی اجازت نہ ہو گی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب مشتری نے دونوں غلاموں پر قبضہ کر لیا تو قبضہ کرنے کی وجہ سے صفقہ تمام ہو گیا کیونکہ خیار عیب کی صورت میں مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر چہ صفقہ مکمل نہیں ہوتا لیکن قبضہ کرنے کے بعد صفقہ مکمل ہو جاتا ہے پس مابعد القبض فقط غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے سے بلاشبہ تفریق صفقہ ہوگا لیکن تفریق صفقہ بعد التمام ہوگا نہ کہ قبل التمام اور تفریق صفقہ قبل التمام اگر چہ نا جائز ہے لیکن تفریق صفقہ بعد التمام جائز ہے اسلئے ہم نے ما بعد القبض فقط غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہے۔ رہا خیار رویت اور خیار شرط تو خیار عیب کو ان پر قیاس کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ خیار رویت اور خیار شرط دونوں کی وجہ سے صفقہ تمام نہیں ہوتا نہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اور نہ قبضہ کرنے کے بعد پس خیار رویت اور خیار شرط کی صورت میں اگر ما بعد القبض بھی ایک غلام واپس کیا اور ایک واپس نہ کیا تو تفریق صفقہ قبل التمام لازم آئے گا۔ حالانکہ یہ نا جائز ہے اور خیار عیب کی صورت میں مابعد القبض اگر ایک غلام واپس کیا اور ایک واپس نہ کیا تو تفریق صفقہ بعد التمام لازم آئے گا اور یہ جائز ہے پس اس قدر فرق کے ساتھ خیار عیب کو خیار رویت اور خیار شرط پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار عیب کی صورت میں مشتری کے دونوں غلاموں پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اگر ایک غلام مستحق ہو گیا یعنی بائع کے علاوہ کسی نے ایک غلام میں استحقاق کا دعویٰ ثابت کر کے اس کو لے لیا تو مشتری بائع سے اس کا حصہ ثمن واپس لے لے لیکن مشتری کو دوسرا غلام واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قبضہ کے بعد تفریق صفقہ بعد التمام لازم آتا ہے اور یہ جائز ہے۔ ہاں اگر قبضہ مبیع سے پہلے ایک غلام مستحق ہو گیا تو مشتری کو دوسرے غلام واپس کرنے کی اجازت ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تفریق صفقہ قبل التمام ہے اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔ پس اس عدم جواز سے بچنے کے لیئے دوسرا غلام بھی واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ (کفایه عنایہ)
He takes (both) or returns both. The proof is that in the case of the option of defect, the contract (safqah) becomes complete after possession of the sold item, but not before possession, as has passed before. So in this issue, the contract will be complete only when the buyer takes possession of both slaves, whereas the buyer has only taken possession of one slave. So the buyer's returning the defective slave and keeping the non-defective one is a division of the contract before completion, and division of the contract before completion is impermissible. And division of the contract within possession is impermissible because possession resembles the contract in that the contract establishes ownership of the corpus (raqabah) of the sold item, and possession establishes ownership of disposition (tasarruf) and ownership of hand (yad). And the purpose of ownership of the corpus is also ownership of disposition and ownership of hand. So it is established that both the contract of sale and possession of sale aim to establish ownership of disposition and ownership of hand. And since both have the same purpose, they resemble each other. And when possession and contract of sale resemble each other, dividing the contract within possession becomes like dividing it within the contract, and division within the contract is impermissible. Therefore, division within possession is also impermissible. The form of division within the contract is that a person said, 'I sold these two slaves for one thousand dirhams,' and the buyer said, 'I accept the sale for one of them.' This is not permissible. Similarly, taking possession of one and returning the other due to defect is impermissible. And if the buyer finds a defect in the slave he has taken possession of, and the other slave he has not taken possession of is free from defect, then there is a difference of opinion among the mashayikh. Thus, it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that the buyer may specifically return the defective slave and take back his share of the price, and not return the non-defective one, because the contract is complete with respect to the possessed slave. So considering the possessed slave, division of the contract does not apply, and when division does not apply, there is no doubt about its permissibility. But the more correct view (al-qawl al-asahh) is that in this case too, the buyer must take both slaves for the full price or return both, because the completion of the contract is linked to taking possession of the sold item; that is, the contract is complete only after the buyer takes possession of the sold item. And 'sold item' is the name for the whole entity on which the contract was made. The contract was made on two slaves, so only after taking possession of both slaves will the contract be complete. In the mentioned case, since he has taken possession of one and not the other, the contract is not complete. And when the contract is not complete, returning one slave inevitably involves dividing the contract before completion, and division of the contract before completion is impermissible. Therefore, in this case too, returning one and not the other is impermissible. And the sold item is the name for the whole entity on which the sale occurred. An analogy for this is that if the seller withholds the sold item because he will deliver it when the buyer pays the price, then the seller's right continues until the buyer pays the full price. So if the buyer pays part of the price, the seller still has the right to withhold the sold item because price is the name for the full consideration, not part of it. Similarly, the sold item is the name for the full counter-value, not part of it. If the buyer takes possession of both slaves and then finds a defect in one of them, he can return only the defective one for his share of the price. Imam Zufar says that in this case too, he must return both or keep both; he does not have the option to return only one. Imam Zufar's proof is that in this case too, there is a division of the contract, even if after completion, and it causes harm to the seller because people usually mix good with bad when selling. So if the buyer is allowed to return one slave, it would harm the seller, because the returned slave would be the bad one and the good one would be kept, making it difficult for the seller to sell the returned defective slave alone. So to prevent harm to the seller, he should not be allowed to return only the defective slave. And this case after possession resembles the case before possession, and the common factor between them is prevention of harm. That is, just as before possession, to prevent harm to the seller, he is not allowed to return only the defective slave, similarly after possession, he is also not allowed to return only the defective slave. And this resembles the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) and the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) – just as in those options, the buyer is not allowed to keep one of two slaves, similarly after possession, he is not allowed to return the defective slave and keep the non-defective one. Our proof is that when the buyer takes possession of both slaves, the contract becomes complete due to possession because in the case of the option of defect, although the contract is not complete before taking possession of the sold item, it becomes complete after possession. So after possession, returning only the defective slave undoubtedly involves a division of the contract, but it is a division after completion, not before. And although division before completion is impermissible, division after completion is permissible. Therefore, we have allowed the buyer after possession to return only the defective slave. As for the option of inspection and option of stipulation, it is not valid to analogize the option of defect to them because in those options, the contract is not completed either before or after possession. Therefore, in those options, if after possession he returns one slave and not the other, division before completion would apply, which is impermissible. In the option of defect, after possession, if he returns one and not the other, division after completion applies, which is permissible. So with this difference, how can one analogize the option of defect to the option of inspection and option of stipulation? The author of Hidayah says that in the case of the option of defect, after the buyer takes possession of both slaves, if one slave becomes subject to a claim (mustahaqq), i.e., someone besides the seller proves a claim to one slave and takes it, then the buyer can take back from the seller his share of the price, but the buyer does not have the option to return the other slave because after possession, division of the contract after completion applies and it is permissible. Yes, if before possession of the sold item, one slave becomes subject to a claim, then the buyer is allowed to return the other slave because in that case there is division of the contract before completion, which is impermissible. So to avoid that impermissibility, he can also return the other slave. (Kifayah, Inayah)
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) in a sale of two slaves. The key issue is whether the buyer, after taking possession of only one slave and finding it defective, can return only that one and keep the other, or must return both. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes based on whether the buyer has taken full possession of all items. Before full possession, the contract (safqah) is not complete, and returning part would be tafriq al-safqah qabl al-tamam, which is invalid. After full possession, the contract is complete, so partial return is permissible (tafriq ba'd al-tamam). The passage presents three positions: Imam Abu Yusuf allowed partial return even when only one slave is possessed, arguing the contract is complete regarding that slave. The more correct view (al-qawl al-asahh) is that partial return is not allowed before full possession. Imam Zufar argued that even after full possession, partial return is not allowed to prevent harm to the seller, analogizing to khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart. The Hanafi response (our proof) rejects Zufar's analogy, emphasizing that in khiyar al-'ayb, possession completes the contract, whereas in the other options, it does not. The passage also discusses the case of a third-party claim (istihqaq) and its effect on partial return. The relied-upon position is that after full possession, the buyer may return only the defective slave, but before full possession, he must return both or keep both.

Key Terms
صفقة (safqah): The contract of exchange in its entirety, including all items sold in one transaction. Completion of safqah depends on possession of all items.
خیار عیب (khiyar al-'ayb): The buyer's option to rescind a sale or claim compensation if a defect is discovered that existed prior to the contract.
تفریق صفقہ (tafriq al-safqah): Dividing the contract of exchange by returning part of the sold items while keeping others. Impermissible if done before the contract is fully completed (by possession of all items).
قبضہ (qabdah): Possession of the sold item. In this context, it is the act of taking physical control of the item, which completes the contract in khiyar al-'ayb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases two slaves for one price. He takes possession of only one and finds it defective. Can he return just that one and keep the other?
A) Yes, according to Imam Abu Yusuf.
B) Yes, according to Imam Zufar.
C) No, according to the correct view, he must return both or keep both.
D) Yes, always.

Key Takeaway
Partial return (tafriq al-safqah) in khiyar al-'ayb is valid only after full possession of all items completes the contract.

Defect in Part of Measured or Weighed Goods: All or Nothing
Stating the rule for defect in part of measured/weighed goods after possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that for homogeneous measured/weighed goods in one container, the buyer must return all or keep all, and distinguish the case of separate containers.

Core Idea
Homogeneous goods in one container are a single unit; you cannot return only the defective part.

When you buy grain or other goods sold by measure or weight, you expect them to be sound. If you discover a defect after taking possession, can you return only the defective portion? In the Hanafi school, the answer depends on whether the goods are in one container or separate ones. This passage from al-Hidayah lays down the rule clearly, preventing partial rescission that would harm the seller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the goods type
Confirm the goods are sold by measure (makil) or weight (mauzun). This rule applies specifically to such items.
2
Check homogeneity
If the goods are of one type (e.g., all wheat), they are considered a single unit. If mixed types, the rule may differ.
Homogeneity means same genus and quality.
3
Count the containers
If all goods are in a single container (e.g., one sack), they are treated as one indivisible unit. If in multiple containers, each container is separate.
The container is the unit of packaging, not the measure.
4
Apply the ruling
For one container: the buyer must return all or keep all; partial return is invalid. For separate containers: only the defective container may be returned.
This rule applies after possession (qabd).
5
Note the rationale
The goods are called by one name (e.g., kurr) and form a single contractual unit. Separating good from bad is not allowed without the seller's consent.
This protects the seller from being left with a mixed lot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اشترى شيئا مما يكال او يوزن فوجد ببعضه عيبا رده كله او اخذه كله و مراده بعد القبض المكيل اذا كان من جنس واحد فهو كشيء واحد الاترى انه يسمى باسم واحد وهو الكر ونحوه وقيل هذا اذا كان في وعاء واحد و ان كان فى وعائين فهو بمنزلة عبدين حتى يرد الوعاء الذي وجد فيه العيب دون الاخر ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے ایسی چیز خریدی جو ناپی جاتی ہے یا وزن کی جاتی ہے پھر اس کا کچھ حصہ عیب دار پایا تو وہ سب واپس کردے یا سب لے لے اور مراد قبضہ کے بعد ہے اسلئے کہ جب مکیلی چیز ایک ہی جنس ہے تو وہ شی واحد کے مانند ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ اس کا ایک ہی نام ہے اور وہ کر ہے اور اس جیسا ہے اور کہا گیا کہ یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ ایک ہی برتن میں ہو اور اگر دو برتنوں میں ہو تو وہ دونوں غلاموں کے مرتبہ میں ہے حتی کہ جس برتن میں عیب پایا اس کو واپس کرے نہ کہ دوسرے کو۔
And whoever buys something that is measured or weighed, then finds a defect in some part of it, he returns all of it or takes all of it. And his (the author's) intent is after possession, because when the measured item is of one type, it is like a single thing. Do you not see that it is called by one name, such as 'kurr' and the like? And it is said that this is when it is in one container. If it is in two containers, then it is like two slaves, so that he returns the container in which the defect is found and not the other. Translation: And the person who bought such a thing that is measured or weighed, then found some portion defective, then he returns all or takes all. And his intent is after possession, because when a measured item is of one type, it is like a single thing. Do you not see that it is called by one name, and that is 'kurr' and the like? And it is said that this is when it is in one container. If it is in two containers, then they are like two slaves, such that he returns the container in which the defect is found and not the other.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Hidayah, explaining the option of defect for goods sold by measure or weight. The general rule: if the goods are homogeneous (same type) and in one container, they are treated as a single unit. Therefore, if a defect is found in part, the buyer must either return the entire lot or keep the entire lot; partial return is not allowed. This rule applies after the buyer has taken possession. However, if the goods are in separate containers, each container is treated as a separate item (like two slaves), so the buyer may return only the defective container. The commentary emphasizes that this ruling is after possession and depends on whether the goods are in one container or multiple containers. The principle is that tafriq al-safqah (partial rescission) is allowed when the items are separate units, but not when they form a single unit. This is a straightforward rule that protects the seller from having to take back a mixed lot where the good and bad are separated.

Key Terms
مکیل (makil): An item sold by measure (e.g., grain).
موزون (mauzun): An item sold by weight (e.g., meat, oil).
وعاء (wi'a): Container. The rule about separate containers applies to items of the same type sold together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a sack of wheat (measured) and finds a defect in a small portion. What must he do?
A) Return only the defective portion.
B) Return the entire sack or keep it all.
C) Keep the whole and claim compensation.
D) Cancel the entire contract.

Key Takeaway
Homogeneous measured/weighed goods in one container are treated as a single unit; partial return is invalid.

Returning a Defective Slave After Possession: The Hanafi Position
Hanafi ruling and proof on returning one defective slave after possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits returning only the defective slave after possession and distinguish this from other khiyar options.

Core Idea
After possession, the contract is complete; dividing it is permissible — this distinguishes khiyar al-'ayb.

When you purchase two items together and later find one defective, can you return just the defective one? The answer depends on the school's view of contract completion. This lesson unpacks a classic dispute between the Hanafis and their opponents, focusing on the role of possession in khiyar al-'ayb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and opposing view
The dispute is whether after taking possession of two slaves, the buyer may return only the defective one. Opponents analogize to khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart, where partial return is impermissible.
The opponents are likely Shafi'is or others who treat all khiyars the same regarding contract division.
2
Understand the opponent's analogy
In khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart, the contract is not completed by possession; thus returning part would divide the contract before completion, which is invalid. Opponents extend this to khiyar al-'ayb.
The analogy is based on the 'illa of incomplete contract.
3
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that in khiyar al-'ayb, possession completes the contract (safqah tammat). Therefore, returning only part after possession divides a completed contract, which is permissible.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) contrasting the nature of the options.
4
Analyze the distinction
The key difference is the effect of possession on contract completion. In khiyar al-'ayb, possession completes; in the other khiyars, it does not. Hence the analogy fails due to different 'illa.
The Hanafi response rejects qiyas because the effective cause varies.
5
Apply to the subsidiary case of istihqaq
If a third party claims one slave before possession, the buyer may return the other (division before completion is avoided). After possession, the buyer cannot return the remaining slave.
This confirms the principle: before possession, the contract is incomplete; after, it is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام کو واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی اور یہ مابعد القبض کی صورت ماقبل القبض کے مشابہ ہوگئی اور ان دونوں کے درمیان جامع دفع ضرر ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بائع سے ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے فقط غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے کی اجازت قبضہ کرنے کے بعد بھی فقط غلام معیب واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے اسی طرح بائع سے ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے قبضہ کرنے کے بعد بھی فقط غلام معیب واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی اور یہ خیار رویت اور خیار شرط کے مشابہ ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح خیار رویت اور مشتری کے واسطے خیار شرط کی وجہ سے دو غلاموں میں سے ایک کو اپنے پاس رکھنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے اسی طرح ما بعد القبض غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے اور غیر معیب کو اپنے پاس رکھنے کی اجازت نہ ہو گی۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب مشتری نے دونوں غلاموں پر قبضہ کر لیا تو قبضہ کرنے کی وجہ سے صفقہ تمام ہو گیا کیونکہ خیار عیب کی صورت میں مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر چہ صلقہ مکمل نہیں ہوتا لیکن قبضہ کرنے کے بعد صفقہ مکمل ہو جاتا ہے پس مابعد القبض فقط غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے سے بلاشبہ تفریق صلقہ ہوگا لیکن تفریق صفقہ بعد التمام ہوگا نہ کہ قبل التمام اور تفریق صفقه قبل التمام اگر چہ نا جائز ہے لیکن تفریق صفقه بعد التمام جائز ہے اسلئے ہم نے ما بعد القبض فقط غلام معیب کو واپس کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہے۔ رہا خیار رویت اور خیار شرط تو خیار عیب کو ان پر قیاس کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ خیار رویت اور خیار شرط دونوں کی وجہ سے صفقہ تمام نہیں ہوتا نہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اور نہ قبضہ کرنے کے بعد پس خیار رویت اور خیار شرط کی صورت میں اگر ما بعد القبض بھی ایک غلام واپس کیا اور ایک واپس نہ کیا تو تفریق صفقہ قبل التمام لازم آئے گا۔ حالانکہ یہ نا جائز ہے اور خیار عیب کی صورت میں مابعد القبض اگر ایک غلام واپس کیا اور ایک واپس نہ کیا تو تفریق صفقه بعد التمام لازم آئے گا اور یہ جائز ہے پس اس قدر فرق کے ساتھ خیار عیب کو خیار رویت اور خیار شرط پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار عیب کی صورت میں مشتری کے دونوں غلامون پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اگر ایک غلام مستحق ہو گیا یعنی بائع کے علاوہ کسی نے ایک غلام میں استحقاق کا دعویٰ ثابت کر کے اس کو لے لیا تو مشتری بائع سے اس کا حصہ ثمن واپس لے لے لیکن مشتری کو دوسرا غلام واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قبضہ کے بعد تفریق صفقہ بعد التمام لازم آتا ہے اور یہ جائز ہے۔ ہاں اگر قبضہ مبیع سے پہلے ایک غلام مستحق ہو گیا تو مشتری کو دوسر اعلام واپس کرنے کی اجازت ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تفریق صفقه قبل التمام ہے اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔ پس اس عدم جواز سے بچنے کے لیئے دوسر اغلام بھی واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ (کفایه عنایہ )
He will not be permitted to return the slave, and this case after possession resembles the case before possession, and the common factor between them is repelling harm. That is, just as before taking possession, to repel harm from the seller, he is only permitted to return the defective slave; similarly, after taking possession, he is not permitted to return only the defective slave. This has become analogous to khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart, i.e., just as in khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart, the buyer cannot keep one of two slaves and return the other, similarly after possession, he cannot return the defective slave and keep the non-defective one. Our proof is that when the buyer took possession of both slaves, the contract is completed because in the case of khiyar al-'ayb, before possession the contract is not complete, but after possession it is complete. Therefore, after possession, returning only the defective slave necessarily causes division of the contract after its completion, not before, and division of the contract before completion is impermissible, but after completion it is permissible. Hence we permitted returning only the defective slave after possession. As for khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart, it is not valid to analogize khiyar al-'ayb to them because the contract is not completed by possession in those cases; thus, after possession, returning one slave would cause division of the contract before completion, which is impermissible. The author of al-Hidayah says: In the case of khiyar al-'ayb, after the buyer takes possession of both slaves, if one slave is claimed by a third party (i.e., someone other than the seller proves ownership and takes it), the buyer takes back his share of the price from the seller, but he does not have the option to return the other slave because after possession, division of the contract after completion occurs and it is permissible. Yes, if one slave is claimed before possession, the buyer has permission to return the other slave because in that case division of the contract is before completion and it is impermissible; to avoid this impermissibility, he may also return the other slave. (Kifayah, Inayah)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the return of a defective slave when two slaves are purchased together. The opponent argues that after possession, returning only the defective slave should not be allowed, analogizing to khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart. The Hanafis respond by distinguishing the cases: in khiyar al-'ayb, the contract is completed upon possession, so returning part of the goods after possession constitutes a division of a completed contract, which is permissible. In khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart, the contract is not completed by possession, so division would be before completion, which is impermissible. The passage also addresses the scenario where one slave is claimed by a rightful owner (istihqaq): after possession, the buyer cannot return the remaining slave; before possession, he may. This ruling is consistent with the principle that division of a completed contract is allowed.

Key Terms
صفقہ (safqah): The contract of sale; its completion or division is the focus of the ruling.
خیار عیب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to return a defective item upon discovery of a defect.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the purchased item.
تفریق صفقہ (tafriq al-safqah): Division of the contract by returning part of the purchased goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, after taking possession of two slaves, if one is found defective, may the buyer return only the defective one?
A) No, because it would divide the contract before completion.
B) Yes, because the contract is complete upon possession, so division is permissible.
C) No, because the seller would suffer harm.
D) Yes, but only if the buyer also returns the other slave.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-'ayb completes the contract upon possession, making partial return permissible, unlike khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Returning Defective Part of Measured or Weighed Goods
Ruling with proof for returning defective part of mikyal/mawzun goods after possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning a defective part of mikyal/mawzun goods after possession, explain the proof based on single entity, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi difference regarding separate containers.

Core Idea
A defective part of mikyal/mawzun goods cannot be returned alone; the whole must be kept or returned as one.

Imagine buying a sack of wheat and finding a defect in only a few grains. Can you return just those grains? The Hanafi school says no — because mikyal and mawzun goods are treated as a single legal entity. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the nature of these goods, and a nuanced difference among Hanafi scholars when the goods are in multiple containers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and timing
Note that the scenario involves a buyer who has already taken possession (بعد القبض) of a mikyal or mawzun item and then discovers a defect in a part of it. The ruling applies only after possession; before possession, the rule is stricter — no partial return at all.
Timing is crucial: after possession, non-mikyal/mawzun items can be partially returned, but mikyal/mawzun cannot.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The buyer must either keep the entire quantity or return the entire quantity. The proof (talil) is that mikyal/mawzun goods of one type are considered one thing (شيء واحد) in both name and legal value. A single grain has no value; the worth lies in the aggregate.
The author uses the example of naming: the whole is called kurr, qafiz, mann, etc.
3
Analyze the reasoning: avoiding the defect of shirkah
If the buyer returns only the defective part, the remaining goods become jointly owned (shirkah) between buyer and seller. This joint ownership in a single sold item is itself a defect (عيبي) that arose from the buyer's side, making it impermissible.
Thus partial return would create a new defect, so the buyer cannot return only part.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
The passage mentions that some later scholars (بعض مشائخ) hold that if the goods are in two separate containers, each container is like a separate slave. In that case, only the defective container may be returned, not the other.
This is a weaker opinion; the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hidayah is that even with multiple containers, the ruling of one entity applies as long as the type is one.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete example
Case: A buyer purchases two bags of iron (mawzun) of the same quality. After possession, he finds one bag is rusty. According to the majority Hanafi position, he cannot return only the rusty bag; he must return both or keep both. The minority view would allow returning only the rusty bag because each bag is separate.
The practical difference depends on whether the goods are considered one entity or multiple.

One who buys something that is measured by volume or weight and finds a defect in part of it may return all of it or take all of it. He said: And whoever buys something that is measured or weighed and finds a defect in part of it, he returns all of it or takes all of it. His meaning is after possession. The measured item, if it is of one type, it is like a single thing. Do you not see that it is called by one name, like kurr and the like? It is said that this is when it is in one container; if in two containers, it is like two slaves, so that he returns the container in which the defect is found, not the other. Translation: And whoever buys something that is measured or weighed, then finds a defect in part of it, he returns all or takes all. The author's meaning is after possession, because when the measured item is of one type, it is like a single thing. Do you not see that it is called by one name, and that is kurr and the like? And it is said that this is when it is in one container; if in two containers, then they are like two slaves, so that he returns the container in which the defect is found, not the other. Explanation: The scenario is that if someone buys a measured item like wheat or a weighed item like iron, then finds a defect in part of it, he has the option to take all or return all. The author of al-Hidayah says that the matn (Imam Muhammad) means that even if the defect is found after possession, the ruling is the same: after possession, if the buyer finds a defect in part of a measured or weighed item, it is not permissible to return only the defective part and keep the rest; rather, he must take all or return all. The condition 'after possession' is mentioned because before possession, the ruling for measured, weighed, and other items is the same: it is absolutely impermissible to return the defective part and keep the rest, whether the item is of the category of mikyal/mawzun or otherwise. After possession, returning the defective part and not returning the rest is permissible for non-mikyal/mawzun items, but not for mikyal/mawzun items. The conclusion is that if someone buys a mikyal/mawzun item, takes possession, then finds a defect in part of it, and it is of one type (e.g., wheat, barley, or iron), the buyer does not have the option to return only the defective part and keep the rest; rather, he must return all or keep all, because due to being one type, it is in the rank of a single thing in terms of name and ruling. In terms of name, it has one name; for example, the entire quantity is called kurr, qafiz, mann, etc. In terms of ruling, it is like a single thing because the value and legal consideration of mikyal/mawzun items depend on the aggregate. A single grain has no value and is not mal mutaqawwim. For this reason, selling a single grain is impermissible. Also, seeing part of a mikyal/mawzun item counts as seeing all, provided the type is one. Thus it is established that a mikyal/mawzun item is in the rank of a single thing with respect to the entire sale. If part is found defective, the buyer must return all or keep all. Because if the buyer returns the defective part and keeps the non-defective part, there would be joint ownership (shirkah) between seller and buyer in the sold item, and joint ownership in a single sold item is also a defect. So the buyer would be returning the defective part with an additional defect (shirkah), and that defect arose from the buyer's side. Therefore, despite an additional defect, how can the buyer be permitted to return the item? So to avoid the defect of shirkah, the buyer must return all or keep all. The author of al-Hidayah says: If the sold item is mikyal/mawzun and of one type, the ruling is as mentioned, whether the item is in one container or two. Some mashayikh hold that the ruling applies only when it is in one container; if it is in two containers, it is like two slaves, meaning that after possession, if the buyer finds a defect in one container, he may return that container specifically and not the other.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof (talil). It addresses the situation where a buyer purchases a commodity sold by volume (mikyal) or weight (mawzun), takes possession, and then finds a defect in a part of it. The ruling is that the buyer must either keep all or return all; he cannot return only the defective part. The proof is that such goods are considered a single entity both in name and in legal treatment. The value is in the aggregate, not in individual units. If only part is returned, joint ownership would arise between buyer and seller, which itself is a defect. The passage also discusses a difference of opinion: some scholars hold that if the goods are in two separate containers, each container is treated like a separate slave, so one may be returned independently. However, the relied-upon position (from the Hidayah) is that even then, the ruling of a single entity applies as long as the type is one.

Key Terms
مکیلی (mikyal): Goods sold by volume (e.g., wheat, barley) that are measured in containers.
موزونی (mawzun): Goods sold by weight (e.g., iron, dates).
شیء واحد (shay' wahid): A single thing; the entire quantity of mikyal/mawzun goods is treated as one legal entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, after possession, what is the ruling if a buyer finds a defect in part of a mikyal item (e.g., wheat) that is of one type?
A) The buyer may return only the defective part.
B) The buyer must either keep all or return all.
C) The buyer may keep the non-defective part and claim a price reduction.
D) The buyer may return the entire item only if the defect is major.

Key Takeaway
For mikyal/mawzun goods of one type, a defective part cannot be returned alone; the whole must be kept or returned to avoid creating a new defect (shirkah).
